The project reflects a commitment to open science, requiring graduate students to release anonymized data and code alongside each published paper. |
| 409 | [EdNet — Large-Scale Hierarchical Dataset in Education](https://github.com/riiid/ednet) | dataset | EdNet is a large-scale dataset of student-system interactions collected over two years by Santa, a multi-platform AI tutoring service with more than 780,000 users in Korea, comprising 131 million interactions from 784,309 students across iOS, Android, and web platforms. The dataset records diverse student actions — including which learning materials were consumed, responses, time spent, and lecture-watching — organized into a four-level hierarchy (KT1 through KT4) of increasing interaction richness. EdNet is described as the largest publicly available education dataset in terms of total students, interactions, and interaction types, and is accompanied by a published paper (arXiv:1912.03072) and an open leaderboard. |
| 411 | [NBER Education Research Data](https://www.nber.org/research/data?page=1&perPage=50&q=education) | dataset | The NBER Public Use Data Archive is a repository of public-use economic, demographic, and enterprise datasets assembled to support NBER-affiliated researchers, including datasets relevant to education such as school district data, birth and natality records, and population survey files. Files are often reformatted for research convenience relative to original sources, and the archive also hosts data and code outputs from NBER research projects intended for replication. Researchers can request that the NBER host data or code from NBER-associated papers, projects, or grants via a formal submission process. |
| 412 | [TALIS — Teaching and Learning International Survey](https://www.oecd.org/education/talis/) | dataset | TALIS is the world's largest international survey about teachers and school leaders. Since 2008, it has gathered information from teachers and school leaders about working conditions and learning environments in over 60 education systems. TALIS 2024 sampled approximately 280,000 teachers in 17,000 schools across 55 education systems. The survey covers ISCED 2 teachers and school leaders, with additional modules for ISCED 1 and ISCED 3, as well as a Teacher Knowledge Survey (TKS) module. A companion survey, TALIS Starting Strong, focuses on early childhood staff and centre leaders. Results are used by policymakers to improve teaching and learning around the world; the next cycle is planned for 2030. |
| 414 | [National Teacher and Principal Survey (NTPS)](https://nces.ed.gov/surveys/ntps/) | dataset | The National Teacher and Principal Survey (NTPS) is a system of related questionnaires that provides descriptive data on the context of public and private elementary and secondary education in the United States. Redesigned from the Schools and Staffing Survey (SASS), NTPS collects information directly from teachers and principals to provide local, state, and national policymakers with statistics on the condition of education. The survey supports analysis of principal, teacher, and student characteristics in detail and enables subgroup analysis (e.g., by gender, race/ethnicity, school locale). Paired with Teacher Follow-up Surveys (TFS) and Principal Follow-up Surveys (PFS), NTPS tracks teacher and principal attrition and mobility. The most recent main collection covered 2020–21, with follow-up surveys in 2021–22. |
| 415 | [National Household Education Surveys Program (NHES)](https://nces.ed.gov/nhes/) | dataset | The National Household Education Surveys Program (NHES) is the flagship household survey program of the National Center for Education Statistics (NCES). It collects nationally representative, descriptive data on the educational activities of children and families in the United States. Surveys are conducted every three to four years on rotating topics; current focus areas include early childhood care and education, parent and family involvement in schools, and homeschooling. Data enable trend analysis over time. The most recent administration concluded in August 2023, with reports released in September 2024 covering early childhood program participation and parent and family involvement in education. |
| 416 | [EDFacts Data Files](https://www2.ed.gov/about/inits/ed/edfacts/index.html) | dataset | EDFacts is a U.S. Department of Education initiative to collect, analyze, and promote the use of high-quality pre-kindergarten through grade 12 data. It centralizes data provided by state education agencies (SEAs), including district and school demographics, program participation, and performance data. EDFacts integrates SEA-supplied performance data with other departmental data assets (such as financial grant information) to support planning, policymaking, and budget decision-making at federal, state, and local levels. The initiative aims to place robust, timely performance data at the core of education decision-making, reduce state and district data reporting burden, and improve state data capabilities through technical assistance. |
| 418 | [Beginning Teacher Longitudinal Study (BTLS)](https://nces.ed.gov/surveys/btls/) | dataset | The Beginning Teacher Longitudinal Study (BTLS) followed a nationally representative cohort of beginning public school teachers first interviewed during the 2007–08 Schools and Staffing Survey through the 2011–12 school year. Unlike typical teacher surveys that provide only a momentary snapshot, BTLS tracked the same cohort over five years to examine career development, attrition, and retention patterns. The study collected data on base salaries, certificate renewals, content area additions, and participation in leadership activities, providing a longitudinal view of early-career teacher trajectories. |
| 419 | [Career and Technical Education Statistics (CTE Stats)](https://nces.ed.gov/surveys/ctes/) | dataset | The Career and Technical Education (CTE) Statistics program delivers comprehensive national data on CTE participation and outcomes from high school through adult and postsecondary education, examining student enrollment patterns, teacher workforce characteristics, and coursetaking by student demographics. The program tracks CTE concentrators across secondary, postsecondary subbaccalaureate, and adult credential programs, and compares their educational trajectories against non-concentrators. Findings from the 2013 high school graduate cohort show CTE concentrators were more likely to earn associate's degrees but less likely to earn bachelor's degrees compared to peers. |
| 420 | [Middle Grades Longitudinal Study of 2017–18 (MGLS:2017)](https://nces.ed.gov/surveys/mgls/) | dataset | The Middle Grades Longitudinal Study of 2017–18 (MGLS:2017) tracked a nationally representative sample of approximately 13,300 sixth-graders across 570 schools to examine the academic, social-emotional, and environmental factors shaping student success and high school readiness during the middle grades transition. Data were collected from five respondent types—students, parents, teachers, special education staff, and school administrators—covering mathematics and reading assessments, executive function, family involvement, and school context. Two collection waves (spring 2018 and spring 2020) followed students through eighth grade, with the second wave shifting to remote participation due to the COVID-19 pandemic; restricted-use files are available to licensed researchers. |
| 421 | [School Pulse Panel (SPP)](https://nces.ed.gov/surveys/spp/) | dataset | The School Pulse Panel (SPP) surveys a nationally representative sample of public K-12 schools on high-priority education topics once a month during the school year, providing near-real-time data on school operations and student outcomes. The program collects information on student attendance rates, academic readiness, tutoring availability, and other operational metrics, with interactive results organized by topic, geography, and school characteristics. Recent findings (June 2025) indicate that 31% of students were reported as behind grade level, 85% of schools offered tutoring services, and the average daily attendance rate was 91%. |
| 424 | [Schools and Staffing Survey (SASS)](https://nces.ed.gov/surveys/sass/) | dataset | The Schools and Staffing Survey (SASS) was an integrated national study of public and private school districts, schools, principals, and teachers designed to provide descriptive data on the context of elementary and secondary education. Conducted seven times between 1987 and 2011, SASS gathered data on teacher demand and compensation, principal and teacher characteristics, school climate, hiring and retention practices, and student demographics. The program was supplemented by the Teacher Follow-Up Survey and Principal Follow-Up Survey tracking mobility and attrition, and was subsequently redesigned and relaunched as the National Teacher and Principal Survey in 2015–16. |
| 425 | [Private School Universe Survey (PSS)](https://nces.ed.gov/surveys/pss/) | dataset | The Private School Universe Survey (PSS) generates biennial data on private schools, teachers, and students in the United States, targeting all institutions not primarily supported by public funds that provide classroom instruction for grades K–12 and employ at least one teacher. Collecting data since 1989–90, the survey gathers information on religious orientation, school level and size, enrollment, high school graduates, gender composition, teacher counts, program emphasis, and kindergarten offerings. The PSS produces data comparable to the Common Core of Data for public schools, enabling cross-sector analysis of enrollment trends including growth patterns in religiously-affiliated schools. |
| 426 | [School Survey on Crime and Safety (SSOCS)](https://nces.ed.gov/surveys/ssocs/) | dataset | The School Survey on Crime and Safety (SSOCS) is the primary source of school-level data on crime and safety for the U.S. Department of Education, collecting information from approximately 4,800 nationally representative public elementary and secondary schools. The survey covers topics related to school crime, violence, discipline, and safety conditions, with periodic data collection and public-use data files available through NCES DataLab. Recent data releases include 2021–22 school year findings alongside historical data through 2019–20, making SSOCS an essential resource for understanding trends in school safety conditions over time. |
| 427 | [High School and Beyond Longitudinal Study (HS&B)](https://nces.ed.gov/surveys/hsb/) | dataset | The High School and Beyond Longitudinal Study (HS&B) is the sixth in a series of NCES longitudinal studies, originally tracking nationally representative cohorts of 10th and 12th graders from 1980 through multiple follow-up surveys to examine how educational system factors influence students' educational and career outcomes. The study collected student and parent questionnaires, cognitive assessments, and high school and postsecondary transcripts, capturing trajectories from high school into the workforce and postsecondary education. Notable findings include associations between advanced high school coursetaking (Algebra II or higher) and lower unemployment at midlife, and data on young adult living arrangements across cohorts. |
| 428 | [National Longitudinal Study of the High School Class of 1972 (NLS-72)](https://nces.ed.gov/surveys/nls72/) | dataset | The National Longitudinal Study of the High School Class of 1972 (NLS-72) pioneered longitudinal research methodology for examining how high school experiences predict career and educational outcomes, following over 21,000 high school seniors through periodic surveys until 1986, with postsecondary transcripts collected in 1984. The study intentionally oversampled schools serving disadvantaged and minority populations and linked educational experiences with early labor market participation and postsecondary enrollment. Findings include that over 90% of participants engaged in paid work within two years of graduation, and the study established a foundational design replicated in subsequent NCES longitudinal programs. |
| 429 | [High School Transcript Studies (HST)](https://nces.ed.gov/surveys/hst/) | dataset | The High School Transcript Studies (HST) collect official academic records from high school students to examine coursetaking patterns and predict future educational outcomes, gathering data on courses taken, credits earned, course sequencing, final grades, class rank, and standardized test scores where available. Transcript data were collected in conjunction with multiple NCES longitudinal studies (HS&B, NELS:88, ELS:2002, HSLS:09) and the National Assessment of Educational Progress (NAEP), spanning collection years from 1982 to 2019. All data are classified using the standardized six-digit Classification of Secondary School Courses coding system and released only as restricted-use files to licensed researchers to protect student confidentiality. |
| 430 | [ED School Climate Surveys (EDSCLS)](https://nces.ed.gov/surveys/edscls/) | dataset | The ED School Climate Surveys (EDSCLS) provide a suite of nationally available survey instruments developed by NCES to measure school climate from multiple stakeholder perspectives, including students, teachers, non-instructional staff, principals, and parents or guardians. The surveys assess school environment across three domains and 13 topics, with a platform enabling schools, districts, and states to collect and report comparable climate data at the local level. NCES has developed psychometric benchmarks supporting meaningful comparisons across student subgroups and institutions, with scores generated at school, district, and state levels. |
| 431 | [Education Finance Statistics Center (EDFIN)](https://nces.ed.gov/edfin/) | dataset | The Education Finance Statistics Center (EDFIN) provides financial information and data on public elementary and secondary education in the United States, collecting annual revenues and expenditures data for public schools and school districts alongside fiscal and nonfiscal trend information. The center offers interactive data tools enabling district-level comparisons, the NCES Financial Handbook, and annual publications on education revenues and expenditures by fiscal year. EDFIN serves as the primary federal source for tracking how public education is funded and where resources are allocated across the nation's school districts. |
| 432 | [Statewide Longitudinal Data Systems (SLDS) Grant Program](https://nces.ed.gov/programs/slds/) | dataset | The Statewide Longitudinal Data Systems (SLDS) Grant Program supports states in designing, developing, implementing, and expanding K-12 and P-20W (early learning through the workforce) longitudinal data systems that enable evidence-based decision-making across educational levels. The program provides grants, technical assistance, publications, webinars, and a State Support Team to help state education agencies build data infrastructure that tracks student progress from early childhood into the workforce. Key resources include best practices guides, a Research Request Process Toolkit, school-level poverty measures, and connections to federal initiatives such as Common Education Data Standards. |
| 433 | [Library Statistics Program](https://nces.ed.gov/surveys/libraries/) | dataset | The Library Statistics Program collects and distributes statistical data on libraries across the U.S. education system, covering academic libraries, public libraries, state library agencies, and elementary/secondary school library media centers. The academic library component was reintegrated into the IPEDS collection as a mandatory annual survey, with data from 2014 onward accessible through the IPEDS Use the Data portal and historical data from 1996–2012 available through dedicated files. The program maintains historical records extending back to 1989 for public libraries, enabling long-term trend analysis of library resources, staffing, and usage across institutional types. |
| 434 | [International Activities Program (IAP)](https://nces.ed.gov/surveys/international/) | dataset | The International Activities Program (IAP) coordinates U.S. participation in large-scale international education studies and assessments to make comparative data available on education and learning across nations. The program administers seven current international studies—including PIRLS, TIMSS, ICILS, PISA, TALIS, PIAAC, and IELS—covering mathematics, science, reading, financial literacy, problem-solving, computer literacy, and adult skills in literacy and numeracy for populations ranging from early childhood through adults aged 16–65. Results typically release 18–24 months after data collection and inform U.S. education policy by contextualizing American student and adult performance within global education systems. |
| 435 | [Education Across America: Cities, Suburbs, Towns, and Rural Areas (Locale Studies)](https://nces.ed.gov/surveys/annualreports/topical-studies/locale) | dataset | The NCES locale studies resource hub, "Education Across America: Cities, Suburbs, Towns, and Rural Areas," compiles comparative data for individuals interested in the condition of education across different geographic locales in the United States. The hub provides tabulations, an interactive "At a Glance" data tool, and indicators spanning family characteristics, educational experiences, school resources and staffing, and educational outcomes across urban, suburban, town, and rural communities. Topics covered include early childhood care, college preparatory coursework, teacher staffing, graduation rates, and postsecondary enrollment, enabling researchers and policymakers to identify geographic disparities in educational opportunity. |
| 436 | [Current Population Survey (CPS) — Education Supplements](https://nces.ed.gov/surveys/cps/) | dataset | The Current Population Survey (CPS) is a monthly household survey of approximately 50,000–60,000 dwelling units conducted by the Bureau of the Census for the Bureau of Labor Statistics, with NCES funding educational supplements since the late 1960s to provide annual data on school enrollment and educational attainment. The survey's October Supplement gathers school enrollment data across elementary, secondary, and postsecondary levels, plus preschool participation, with supplementary items covering language proficiency, disabilities, computer use and access, student mobility, and private school tuition. The CPS employs a multistage stratified sampling scheme with households rotating in-sample for four months, out for eight, and back for four more, producing nationally representative estimates of the civilian noninstitutionalized population. |
| 437 | [International Civic and Citizenship Education Study (ICCS)](https://www.iea.nl/studies/iea/iccs) | dataset | ICCS is the largest international study dedicated to civic and citizenship education, assessing Grade 8 students' civic knowledge, beliefs, attitudes, and behaviors related to democratic participation. The study also collects contextual data on curriculum, teaching practices, and school climate, with cycles in 2009, 2016, and 2022, and a fully digital 2027 cycle in progress. ICCS data serve as the primary evidence source for UN Sustainable Development Goal indicator 4.7.4 on global citizenship understanding. |
| 438 | [International Computer and Information Literacy Study (ICILS)](https://www.iea.nl/studies/iea/icils) | dataset | ICILS measures how well Grade 8 students across multiple educational systems are prepared for study, work, and life in a digital world, assessing computer and information literacy (CIL) including the knowledge and skills needed to use technology for investigation, creation, and communication. The study has run in 2013, 2018, and 2023 cycles, with a 2028 cycle currently underway, and supports monitoring of UN SDG targets and EU education priorities. Contextual data on students' home and school technology environments are collected alongside achievement scores. |
| 440 | [Responses to Educational Disruption Survey (REDS)](https://www.iea.nl/data-tools/repository/REDS) | dataset | REDS examined the impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on lower secondary education (Grade 8) across 11 nations including Burkina Faso, Denmark, Ethiopia, India, Kenya, Rwanda, Slovenia, the UAE, Uruguay, and Uzbekistan, with data collected between December 2020 and July 2021. The survey gathered internationally comparable responses from 21,063 students, 15,004 teachers, and 1,581 school principals, enabling cross-national analysis of pandemic-related educational disruption. The dataset is available in SAS and SPSS formats through the IEA Data Repository and is citable via DOI (https://doi.org/10.58150/REDS_2021_data). |
| 442 | [Education Stabilization Fund (ESF) COVID-19 Relief Data](https://covid-relief-data.ed.gov) | dataset | The Education Stabilization Fund data portal tracks over $276 billion in federal COVID-19 education relief awarded across four programs: Elementary and Secondary School Emergency Relief (ESSER, $189.5B), Higher Education Emergency Relief (HEER, $75.2B), Emergency Assistance to Non-Public Schools (EANS, $5.5B), and Governor's Emergency Education Relief (GEER, $4.3B). The portal provides grantee-level expenditure data searchable by state, district, and institution, with bulk downloads of annual performance report datasets and a public API. Data covers over 16,000 school districts and 4,500 colleges and universities through the reporting period ending January 2026. |
| 443 | [ASSISTments 2012-13 School Data with Affect](https://sites.google.com/site/assistmentsdata/datasets/2012-13-school-data-with-affect) | dataset | A large-scale log of approximately 10 million student problem-solving interactions from the ASSISTments intelligent tutoring system during the 2012-2013 school year, augmented with machine-learning predictions of four affective states per interaction — frustration, confusion, engagement/concentration, and boredom — scored on a 0-to-1 scale. Records include student attempts, hint requests, response times, problem metadata, skill tags, and classroom/school identifiers, enabling research on the relationship between student affect and math learning outcomes in K-12 settings. |
| 444 | [ASSISTments Skill-Builder Data 2009-2010](https://sites.google.com/site/assistmentsdata/home/2009-2010-assistment-data/skill-builder-data-2009-2010) | dataset | Student interaction logs from ASSISTments skill-builder problem sets used in K-12 mathematics during the 2009-2010 school year, structured as one row per student-problem attempt. Each skill-builder focuses on a single mathematics skill (with optional multi-skill tagging) and requires students to answer three consecutive questions correctly before moving on; the dataset captures correctness, hint usage, and response sequences under this mastery criterion. A corrected, deduplicated version is available via Google Drive alongside the original CSV. |
| 445 | [Literacy and Numeracy Assessment (LaNA)](https://www.iea.nl/studies/iea/LaNA) | dataset | LaNA is an international assessment of emerging mathematics and reading comprehension skills at the end of primary school (grades 4–6 depending on context), designed for countries that need timely, reliable, nationally representative, and internationally comparable education data. It is grounded in and linked to TIMSS and PIRLS, using the same benchmarks to track progress toward SDG Indicator 4.1.1b. The study collects contextual information about resources, learning experiences, and school environments alongside achievement data. Six countries have administered LaNA: Burkina Faso, Egypt, Nigeria, Pakistan, Palestinian National Authority, and Senegal, with earlier pilots in Haiti, North Macedonia, Punjab (Pakistan), and Serbia. Initial administrations occurred in 2016–2020 (pilots) and 2023 (linking study). |
| 446 | [TIMSS Advanced](https://www.iea.nl/data-tools/repository/timssadvanced) | dataset | TIMSS Advanced assesses students in their final year of secondary school who are enrolled in advanced mathematics and physics programs. It is the only international assessment measuring student readiness for university-level STEM studies, gathering policy-relevant data on curriculum emphasis, technology use, and teacher preparation to support education reform and STEM policy planning. Data from three cycles are available through the IEA repository in SAS and SPSS formats: 1995, 2008, and 2015. Each dataset is assigned a DOI for citation purposes. |
| 447 | [TIMSS Longitudinal](https://www.iea.nl/data-tools/repository/timsslongitudinal) | dataset | TIMSS Longitudinal is an optional extension of TIMSS 2023 that measures student learning gains over one year of schooling by assessing the same cohort at two points in time. It targets students in grades 4–5 and grades 8–9, capturing growth in mathematics and science achievement across a critical schooling period. Data from the 2023 and 2024 collections are publicly available in SAS, SPSS, and R formats through the IEA data repository, with DOI citations provided for academic use. |
| 448 | [CIVED — Civic Education Study](https://www.iea.nl/data-tools/repository/cived) | dataset | CIVED was an international assessment covering the content domains of democracy and citizenship, national identity, and social cohesion and diversity. Described as the largest and most rigorous study of civic education conducted internationally at the time, it assessed students at grades 8 and 12. Phase 1 of the study ran from 1996–1997 and Phase 2 from 1999–2000. Datasets for the 1999 assessment cycles at both grade levels are publicly available in SAS and SPSS formats through the IEA data repository. CIVED is the predecessor to ICCS, which continues civic education measurement in subsequent cycles. |
| 452 | [Service Delivery Indicators Education Survey 2014 — Tanzania](https://microdata.worldbank.org/index.php/catalog/2748) | dataset | This World Bank dataset examines primary education service delivery quality across Tanzania through a 2014 survey of 400 primary schools. It captures three standardized indicator categories: teacher effort (school and classroom absence rates, daily teaching time), teacher knowledge (subject matter competency in English, mathematics, and pedagogy), and availability of inputs (infrastructure, textbooks, equipment, and pupil-teacher ratios). The dataset also includes direct grade-4 student assessments in language, mathematics, and non-verbal reasoning, and is harmonized to enable cross-country comparisons within the broader Service Delivery Indicators initiative covering Sub-Saharan Africa. |
| 453 | [National Longitudinal Study of Adolescent to Adult Health (Add Health), 1994–2025](https://www.icpsr.umich.edu/web/ICPSR/studies/21600) | dataset | Add Health is a nationally representative longitudinal panel study tracking a cohort of U.S. adolescents from grades 7–12 (1994–95) through early midlife, with data collection across six waves extending to 2025 when participants were ages 39–51. The study combines survey data on social, economic, psychological, and physical well-being with rich contextual information on families, schools, neighborhoods, and peer and romantic relationships; later waves add biospecimens, physical measurements, and comprehensive life history data. It is one of the largest and most widely cited longitudinal datasets in U.S. education and adolescent development research, supporting studies of school transitions, educational attainment, and long-term health and socioeconomic outcomes. |
| 454 | [WPI — ASSISTments Math 2004–2005 (912 Students)](https://pslcdatashop.web.cmu.edu/DatasetInfo?datasetId=92) | dataset | A public dataset in the PSLC DataShop repository containing interaction logs from 912 students using the ASSISTments intelligent tutoring system during the 2004–2005 academic year. The dataset, contributed by PI Neil Heffernan (Worcester Polytechnic Institute), records student problem-solving transactions in middle-school mathematics. It is one of three ASSISTments datasets in DataShop spanning 2004–2007, with this cohort containing approximately 580,785 transactions. Part of the WPI–ASSISTments project (DataShop ID 92), listed as a public project accessible to registered DataShop users. |
| 455 | [WPI — ASSISTments Math 2005–2006 (3136 Students)](https://pslcdatashop.web.cmu.edu/DatasetInfo?datasetId=120) | dataset | A public PSLC DataShop dataset capturing 3,136 students' interactions with the ASSISTments intelligent tutoring platform during the 2005–2006 school year, contributed by PI Neil Heffernan. ASSISTments provides students with scaffolded math problem-solving practice while simultaneously collecting fine-grained transaction-level data (student responses, hints requested, errors made) suitable for knowledge component modeling and learning curve analysis. This dataset (DataShop ID 120) contains approximately 1,451,003 transactions — the largest of the three ASSISTments cohorts in DataShop. Listed as a public project on the DataShop catalog. |
| 456 | [Geometry Area (1996–97)](https://pslcdatashop.web.cmu.edu/DatasetInfo?datasetId=76) | dataset | One of the oldest and most widely used benchmark datasets in educational data mining, this public PSLC DataShop dataset records students' interactions with a Geometry Area Cognitive Tutor during the 1996–97 academic year. PI Ken Koedinger (CMU). The dataset has been assigned a persistent DOI (10.60710/DATASET-76) as part of DataShop's April 2026 DOI release. It has been used in numerous learning science and EDM studies and was featured as the standard teaching dataset for the EDM Summer School 2017 (DataShop ID 2174). Subject area: Math/Geometry. Listed as a public project. |
| 458 | [Junyi Academy Math Practicing Log (to January 2015)](https://pslcdatashop.web.cmu.edu/DatasetInfo?datasetId=1198) | dataset | A public PSLC DataShop dataset contributed by PI Haw-Shiuan Chang capturing student math practice logs from Junyi Academy, a Taiwanese e-learning platform described as functionally similar to Khan Academy. The dataset records student interactions with mathematics exercises through January 2015 and is available in full (DataShop ID 1198) and partial-sample (DataShop ID 1275) versions. Subject area: Math/Other. Listed as a public project, this large-scale log dataset from a deployed online platform is suited for studies of learning trajectories, knowledge component modeling, and engagement in self-paced digital learning environments. |
| 459 | [Adapterrex — Erroneous Examples Studies (2011–2019)](https://pslcdatashop.web.cmu.edu/DatasetInfo?datasetId=495) | dataset | A public collection of 10 datasets from the Adapterrex project, contributed by PI Bruce McLaren (CMU), investigating the learning benefits of erroneous examples versus conventional problem-solving in middle-school mathematics. Studies ran from Fall 2011 through Spring 2019 across multiple school sites (Hopewell, Steel Valley, and others), with transaction counts ranging from approximately 4,300 to 376,000 per dataset. The research used randomized controlled designs (ErrEx vs. PS conditions) to examine whether studying worked examples containing deliberate errors improves conceptual understanding and transfer. DataShop IDs 495, 534, 579, 586, 592, 659, 1307, 2223, 2648, 2996. Listed as a public project. |
| 460 | [Blocked vs. Interleaved Instruction — Fraction Arithmetic](https://pslcdatashop.web.cmu.edu/DatasetInfo?datasetId=1190) | dataset | A public PSLC DataShop dataset contributed by PI Rony Patel examining the effects of blocked versus interleaved practice on fraction arithmetic (addition and multiplication) learning. Two datasets are available: DS1190 (Fraction Addition and Multiplication, April 2015–August 2016, ~24,453 transactions) and DS1706 (Blocked vs. Interleaved condition comparison, August 2016–March 2018, ~365,312 transactions). Subject area: Math/Other. The datasets support analysis of how the sequencing of different problem types during practice affects learning outcomes, a topic with strong relevance to instructional design and spacing/interleaving research. |
| 461 | [iSnap — Introductory Programming (2015–2018)](https://pslcdatashop.web.cmu.edu/DatasetInfo?datasetId=1920) | dataset | A public collection of seven datasets capturing students' block-based programming interactions with iSnap, a logging-enabled fork of the Snap! visual programming environment, contributed by PI Thomas Price (NC State University). Data spans Fall 2015 through Spring 2018 (DataShop IDs 1920, 1921, 1922, 2517, 2724, 2738, 5667) with per-semester transaction counts ranging from approximately 84,000 to 208,000. iSnap records detailed step-by-step programming actions — code edits, hint requests, and project states — enabling fine-grained analysis of novice programming behavior, hint-seeking strategies, and knowledge component modeling for introductory CS education. | 464 | [Education at a Glance (EAG)](https://www.oecd.org/en/publications/serials/education-at-a-glance_g1gha6b0.html) | dataset | Education at a Glance is OECD's authoritative annual statistical compendium on education systems worldwide, published each September. Each edition provides more than 100 internationally harmonised indicators covering the output of educational institutions; the impact of learning on earnings and employment; access, participation, and progression through education levels; financial resources invested in education; and teachers, learning environments, and school organisation. Data are drawn from the joint UNESCO-OECD-Eurostat (UOE) administrative data collection and from OECD's own surveys (PISA, TALIS, PIAAC), and cover OECD member countries plus a range of partner economies. The 2025 edition (released September 2025, 542 pages) is the most recent. Researchers use EAG as the primary cross-national reference for structural and system-level education indicators. |
| 465 | [PISA for Development (PISA-D)](https://www.oecd.org/en/data/datasets/pisa-d-pisa-for-development.html) | dataset | PISA for Development (PISA-D) is an adapted version of the PISA assessment designed to support low- and middle-income countries in using internationally comparable assessment data to monitor progress toward national targets and SDG 4. PISA-D uses the same proficiency scales as standard PISA but adds more granular performance descriptors at the lower end of the scale, enhanced questionnaire instruments relevant to developing-country contexts, and — uniquely — an out-of-school component assessing 14–16-year-olds who are not enrolled. Nine countries participated in the school-based assessment (Bhutan, Cambodia, Ecuador, Guatemala, Honduras, Paraguay, Senegal, Zambia); five conducted the out-of-school assessment (Guatemala, Honduras, Panama, Paraguay, Senegal). School-based results were released December 2018; out-of-school results in 2020. Public-use files in SAS and SPSS formats are freely downloadable and include student, principal, teacher, parent, and out-of-school respondent records, codebooks, questionnaires, and data compendia. |
| 467 | [Survey on Social and Emotional Skills (SSES)](https://www.oecd.org/en/about/programmes/oecd-survey-on-social-and-emotional-skills.html) | dataset | The OECD Survey on Social and Emotional Skills (SSES) is the largest global initiative to gather comparable cross-national data on the social and emotional skill development of 10- and 15-year-old students. The survey measures a broad set of skills organised into five domains: task performance (persistence, responsibility, self-control, achievement motivation), emotional regulation (stress resistance, emotional control, optimism), engaging with others (assertiveness, sociability, energy), open-mindedness (curiosity, creativity, tolerance), and collaboration. Contextual data are collected from students, teachers, school principals, and (optionally) parents. Round 1 (2019) covered 10 cities/regions; Round 2 (2023) expanded to 16 sites across six countries and ten sub-national entities — including Bulgaria, Chile, Peru, Spain, Mexico, Ukraine, and cities in Colombia, India, UAE, Italy, Japan, Finland, China, Indonesia, and Brazil — surveying approximately 18,000 ten-year-olds and 52,000 fifteen-year-olds. Datasets for both rounds are available on request from OECD. The SSES 2023 database page and 2019 database page provide application and access details. |
| 468 | [OECD Online Education Database (UOE)](https://search.oecd.org/education/database.htm) | dataset | The OECD Online Education Database is the annual administrative data collection underpinning Education at a Glance indicators. Conducted jointly by OECD, the UNESCO Institute for Statistics, and Eurostat (the UOE joint data collection), it has run in its current form since 1993. The collection comprises approximately 25 electronic questionnaires covering student enrolments (nine questionnaires), student entrants (four), graduates (three), personnel (three), education finance (three), class sizes (two), and general population data (one). Data are reported by Ministries of Education or national statistical offices according to international standards and the ISCED classification. Indicators derived from UOE cover educational outputs, access, participation and progression, human and financial resources invested in education, and structural features of national education systems. Raw UOE data are available through the OECD Education data portal and through the OECD.Stat platform; methodological guidance is provided in the UOE Data Collection Manual. |
| 469 | [IDEA Section 618 Data](https://www.ed.gov/data/idea-section-618-data) | dataset | The IDEA Section 618 Data portal collects and publishes annual data on children and youth with disabilities receiving federally mandated special education services under the Individuals with Disabilities Education Act (IDEA). Coverage spans infants and toddlers (birth through age 2) served under Part C early intervention programs, and children ages 3–21 served under Part B special education programs. A searchable database allows users to retrieve state-submitted datasets by year and category; additional data notes and downloadable products are linked to ED's Open Data Platform at data.ed.gov. |
| 471 | [Condition of Education](https://nces.ed.gov/programs/coe) | dataset | The Condition of Education is NCES's flagship annual report presenting key education indicators across all levels of the U.S. system, from early childhood through postsecondary education and into the labor market. The 2024 edition covers six major topic areas — family characteristics, elementary and secondary education, postsecondary enrollment and outcomes, employment and earnings by educational attainment, international comparisons, and school crime and safety — with data updated throughout the year as new sources become available. Indicators are accessible as interactive web pages organized by topic and demographic subgroup, with PDF archives dating back to 1989. |
| 472 | [Digest of Education Statistics](https://nces.ed.gov/programs/digest/) | dataset | The Digest of Education Statistics is an annual NCES compendium spanning the full breadth of American education from prekindergarten through graduate school. It aggregates data from both government and private sources on schools, colleges, teachers, enrollments, graduates, educational attainment, finances, and federal funding, supplemented by population trends, labor force characteristics, and international comparisons. Current tables and historical versions are available online back to 1995, with PDF archives from 1990–2020; a new Digest State Dashboard provides state-level interactive profiles for all 50 states, D.C., territories, and the Bureau of Indian Education. |
| 473 | [Education Recovery Project — COVID Learning Loss Data](https://edopportunity.org/recovery/data) | dataset | A national dataset tracking pandemic-related learning loss and recovery across U.S. school districts in reading and math from 2019 to 2024, released by Stanford's Educational Opportunity Project (SEDA 2024.2, updated February 2026). As of spring 2024, U.S. students remained nearly half a grade level behind pre-pandemic achievement in both subjects; the data also captures the impact of remote learning policies and federal pandemic relief funding on district-level recovery trajectories. Download requires a data use agreement; raw files are available for independent analysis alongside an interactive district-level explorer. |
| 474 | [Segregation Tracking Project — School and Neighborhood Segregation Data](https://edopportunity.org/segregation/data) | dataset | A multi-decade dataset tracking racial/ethnic and economic segregation across U.S. schools and neighborhoods, available at the state, county, metropolitan area, and school-district level (version 2.0, updated February 2026). Underlying research analyzes patterns from 1991 to 2020 and finds that school segregation has increased over the past three decades, particularly in large urban districts, driven substantially by policy choices. Raw data are downloadable under a data use agreement alongside an interactive mapping explorer and peer-reviewed methods documentation. |
| 475 | [District Court Order Desegregation Data](https://cepa.stanford.edu/data/district-court-order-data) | dataset | A dataset cataloging all medium-to-large U.S. school districts ever placed under a court-ordered desegregation plan, covering 358 court cases affecting 850 school districts plus 207 HEW actions since 1978. Each record includes case name, state, NCES district ID, year of initial case, current plan status, and dismissal date; data were compiled from case dockets, Department of Justice records, NAACP Legal Defense materials, and U.S. Department of Education files and verified against Westlaw. Available in Stata (versions 12 and 15), Excel, SAS 7, and SPSS formats; last updated February 2021 with revised dismissal statuses. |
| 476 | [Opportunity Atlas — Neighborhood-Level Economic Mobility Data](https://opportunityinsights.org/paper/the-opportunity-atlas/) | dataset | A publicly available dataset built from anonymized longitudinal records covering nearly the entire U.S. population, tracking outcomes for children from the 1984–1989 birth cohorts (measured at approximately age 35) by Census tract, county, commuting zone, and national level. Measures include household income, incarceration rates, and neighborhood characteristics, all stratified by parental income percentile, race, and gender. Data files are downloadable in Stata and Excel formats from the Opportunity Insights website, with a full replication package on Harvard Dataverse (DOI: 10.7910/DVN/NALG3E) and an interactive tool at opportunityatlas.org. |
| 479 | [Social Capital Atlas — County, ZIP, High School, and College Data](https://opportunityinsights.org/paper/social-capital-i-measurement-and-associations-with-economic-mobility/) | dataset | A dataset measuring three dimensions of social capital — economic connectedness between high- and low-SES individuals, social cohesion (clique formation in friendship networks), and civic engagement (volunteering rates) — derived from analysis of 21 billion Facebook friendships. Data are available at the county, ZIP code, high school, and college levels, including a 100×100 friending-rate matrix across socioeconomic groups, enabling research on which communities provide cross-class social ties that support upward income mobility. All files are freely downloadable in CSV format from opportunityinsights.org/data/ with an interactive Social Capital Atlas at socialcapital.org. |
| 480 | [Who Becomes an Inventor — Innovation Rates by Childhood Location and Demographics](https://opportunityinsights.org/paper/losteinsteins/) | dataset | A dataset tracking more than one million U.S. inventors by linking patent records to tax records and school district records, providing innovation rates organized by childhood commuting zone and state, gender, parental income quintile, educational institution attended, and career trajectory including income distributions. The data reveal that children from high-income families are significantly more likely to become inventors, largely due to exposure to innovation rather than innate ability — the so-called "lost Einsteins" phenomenon. Available in Stata, Excel, and README formats as individual tables and a bundled ZIP, with a full replication package on Harvard Dataverse. |
| 481 | [Race and Economic Opportunity — Intergenerational Mobility by Race](https://opportunityinsights.org/paper/race/) | dataset | A dataset derived from de-identified longitudinal records covering nearly the entire U.S. population from 1989 to 2015, measuring intergenerational income mobility and related outcomes disaggregated by race, gender, and parental income percentile at the national, commuting zone, and county levels. Data tables include national statistics by parent income percentile and race, income transition matrices, and estimates for second-generation immigrants by country of origin, as well as intergenerational educational attainment matrices. Files are downloadable in Stata and Excel formats; a full replication package is available on GitHub and Harvard Dataverse. |
| 482 | [Changing Opportunity — County and Commuting Zone Trend Data (1978–1992 Cohorts)](https://opportunityinsights.org/paper/changingopportunity/) | dataset | A dataset covering birth cohorts from 1978 to 1992 at the county, commuting zone, and national levels, tracking trends in earnings, educational attainment, standardized test scores, and mortality rates by parental income, race, and gender over time. The data document growing class gaps and shrinking race gaps in economic opportunity across these cohorts and include a crosswalk converting income percentiles to 2023 dollars. All tables are freely downloadable in CSV and Stata formats with PDF codebooks from the Opportunity Insights website. |
| 483 | [Geography of Intergenerational Mobility — Commuting Zone and County Data](https://opportunityinsights.org/paper/land-of-opportunity/) | dataset | A foundational dataset analyzing intergenerational income mobility using administrative records from more than 40 million children and their parents, covering commuting zones, counties, and metropolitan statistical areas across the United States. In addition to mobility statistics and income transition matrices, the dataset includes community characteristics correlated with upward mobility — school quality, segregation levels, income inequality, social capital, and family stability — supporting causal analysis of place effects on children's outcomes. Data are available in Excel and Stata formats (10 online tables) with a bundled replication package; full dataset on Harvard Dataverse (DOI: 10.7910/DVN/NALG3E). |
| 484 | [NSC High School Benchmarks — Postsecondary Outcomes Data Appendix](https://nscresearchcenter.org/high-school-benchmarks/) | dataset | An annually updated Excel data appendix accompanying the NSC High School Benchmarks report (13th edition in 2025), providing postsecondary enrollment, first-year persistence, and six-year credential completion rates for three high school graduating classes (2024, 2022, and 2018 respectively). Outcomes are disaggregated by high school characteristics including income level, minority enrollment percentage, and geographic locale, enabling comparisons between high- and low-poverty schools; for example, STEM completion rates ranged from 8.1% at high-poverty schools to 22.4% at low-poverty schools for the class of 2018. The 2025 data appendix is directly downloadable as an XLSX file from the report page, with prior-year appendices available back to at least 2022. |
| 486 | [Urban Institute Education Data Portal — API Documentation and Data Sources](https://educationdata.urban.org/documentation/) | dataset | The full API documentation for the Urban Institute's Education Data Portal, which harmonizes and provides unified programmatic access to six major federal education datasets: the Common Core of Data (CCD) school directory and enrollment data, the Civil Rights Data Collection, the Small Area Income and Poverty Estimates, IPEDS postsecondary institution data, the College Scorecard, and the National Historical Geographic Information System (NHGIS). The API supports queries by education level (schools, districts, colleges), geography, time frame, and indicator; code interfaces are available for Stata, R, Python, and JavaScript. Data are openly accessible without authentication for most endpoints; the documentation page lists all currently available endpoints and variables. |
| 487 | [Current Population Survey (CPS) Data at NBER](https://www.nber.org/research/data/current-population-survey-cps-data-nber) | dataset | The NBER's maintained archive of the U.S. Current Population Survey, the federal government's primary monthly survey of labor force participation and employment, spanning basic monthly data from 1976 to the present and CPS supplements from 1964 onward. The archive includes the Merged Outgoing Rotation Groups (MORG) files for earnings analysis, the Mare-Winship standardized subsets (1964–1992), and thematic supplement extracts covering schooling, fertility, immigration, and income — making it a key source for longitudinal analysis of educational attainment and its labor market returns. All files are freely downloadable from the NBER website with SAS, SPSS, and Stata data definition files and comprehensive methodology documentation. |

| 512 | [Teaching Teachers to Use Computer Assisted Learning Effectively: Experimental and Quasi-Experimental Evidence](https://www.nber.org/papers/w32388) | paper | Examines a program providing weekly coaching to help educators implement computer-assisted learning for customized student progress in elementary and middle school mathematics. Two field experiments showed significant gains of 0.12-0.22 standard deviations in math performance. The research reveals that meaningful improvements occurred when students received at least 35 minutes of weekly practice, with success factors including strong teacher buy-in, clear implementation timing, and consistent monitoring of student progress with targeted intervention for struggling learners. |

| 573 | [SpellRead](https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/481) | report | SpellRead (formerly SpellRead Phonological Auditory Training) is a reading intervention for grade 2 and above that integrates auditory and visual reading processes through systematic, explicit instruction, teaching students to recognize and manipulate English sounds and practice skills using appropriately leveled texts. Sample characteristics across qualifying studies included 45% White, 16% Black, and 40% Hispanic students, with 45% receiving free/reduced-price lunch. |
| 596 | [TNTP Teaching Fellows](https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/675) | report | TNTP Teaching Fellows is a selective alternative teacher certification program that recruits career changers and uncertified recent graduates, providing online coursework and 5–7 weeks of in-person training focused on foundational teaching skills, plus ongoing professional development in the first year, targeting middle and high school instruction in grades 6–12. The WWC reviewed 8 eligible studies, with 1 meeting standards, and found no discernible effects on mathematics achievement for middle and high school students. The lack of a tier assignment reflects insufficient qualifying evidence to establish a formal evidence tier. |
| 597 | [I CAN Learn Algebra](https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/677) | report | I CAN Learn Algebra is a computer-based math curriculum for secondary students — including middle school, high school, and college — that provides mathematics instruction through a series of interactive lessons that students work on individually at their own computers. The WWC reviewed 12 eligible studies, with 1 meeting standards, and found no discernible effects on general mathematics achievement for secondary students, with a Tier 0 evidence classification indicating insufficient qualifying research. The limited qualifying evidence limits what can be concluded about the program's effectiveness compared to its wide usage. |
| 598 | [Prentice Hall/Pearson Literature (2007–2015)](https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/682) | report | Prentice Hall/Pearson Literature (2007–2015) is an English language arts curriculum for grades 6–12 using passages from fiction, nonfiction, poetry, and digital media, with online components for personalized assignments and progress monitoring to build general literacy achievement and comprehension. The WWC reviewed 3 qualifying studies and found no discernible effects on general literacy achievement and comprehension for adolescent readers, with evaluations covering grades 7–10 for comprehension and grades 7–9 for literacy achievement. The no-discernible-effects finding is notable for a widely adopted commercial ELA curriculum at the secondary level. |
| 599 | [Accelerated Math — Primary Mathematics](https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/684) | report | Accelerated Math is a software tool by Renaissance Learning for grades K–12 that provides individualized practice problems, scores student work automatically, and generates progress reports to help teachers differentiate mathematics instruction, reviewed here for primary mathematics in grades 2–9. The WWC reviewed 24 eligible studies, with 6 meeting standards, and found mixed effects on mathematics test scores in primary courses, indicating inconsistent evidence of impact. The large research base with mixed results suggests that implementation context and fidelity may play a significant role in whether the intervention produces gains. |
| 600 | [NBPTS Certification — Student Achievement](https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/689) | report | National Board for Professional Teaching Standards (NBPTS) Certification awards professional certification to educators whose teaching practices meet established standards for accomplished teaching, requiring a computer-based assessment and three portfolio entries completed over 1 to 5 years, evaluated here for effects on student achievement in grades 3–8. The WWC reviewed 39 eligible studies, with 5 meeting standards, and found no discernible effects on English language arts achievement and mixed effects on general mathematics achievement. The large number of eligible studies and varied results point to significant heterogeneity in how board certification relates to student outcomes across contexts. |
| 601 | [Achieve3000 — Beginning Reading Fluency](https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/692) | report | Achieve3000 is a supplemental online literacy program providing differentiated nonfiction reading content to students in grades preK–12, building phonemic awareness, phonics, fluency, comprehension, vocabulary, and writing through instruction tailored to each student's reading ability, reviewed here for beginning readers in grades 2–3. The WWC reviewed 2 eligible studies, with 1 meeting standards, and found no discernible effects on reading fluency for beginning readers. The no-discernible-effects finding in the beginning reading context suggests the program may be better suited to its adolescent literacy applications reviewed under a separate report. |
| 602 | [Passport Reading Journeys](https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/697) | report | Passport Reading Journeys is a supplemental curriculum for grades 6–12 combining teacher-led instruction with technology to enhance reading comprehension, vocabulary, word study, and writing skills for struggling readers, organized around themed two-week instructional sequences with whole-class and small-group lessons, independent reading, videos, and computer-based practice. The WWC reviewed 6 eligible studies, with 3 meeting standards, and found mixed effects on reading comprehension (grades 6–9) and no discernible effects on general literacy achievement (grades 6–9). The research sample was predominantly Black (67%) and economically disadvantaged (87% free/reduced-price lunch eligible). |
| 603 | [Word Generation](https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/704) | report | Word Generation is a supplemental program for grades 4–8 that builds students' vocabulary, academic language, and perspective-taking skills through classroom discussion and debate, using interdisciplinary units with daily lessons centered on high-interest topics, with variants including WordGen Weekly and subject-specific editions in science and social studies. The WWC reviewed 5 eligible studies, with 1 meeting standards, and found no discernible effects on either reading comprehension or English language proficiency, with all qualifying studies involving 100% English learner populations. Despite its design rationale for academic language development, the program did not demonstrate measurable gains on the evaluated outcome domains. |
| 604 | [Literacy Design Collaborative (LDC)](https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/711) | report | Literacy Design Collaborative (LDC) provides professional development, coaching, and resources to support teachers working collaboratively in their schools to design and implement high-quality, standards-aligned literacy instruction materials focused on reading, research, and writing skills for students in grades 4–8. The WWC reviewed 5 eligible studies, with 3 meeting standards, and found mixed effects on general literacy achievement and no discernible effects on general social studies achievement. The mixed literacy finding across a relatively robust evidence base (3 qualifying studies) suggests LDC may be effective for some implementation contexts but not consistently across all schools. |
| 605 | [Promoting Alternative Thinking Strategies (PATHS)](https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/712) | report | Promoting Alternative Thinking Strategies (PATHS) is an elementary curriculum for grades 1–5 that delivers short lessons focused on self-control, emotional literacy, social competence, positive peer relations, and interpersonal problem-solving skills to enhance social-emotional competencies and reduce aggression and behavior problems. The WWC reviewed 13 eligible studies, with 2 meeting standards, and found no discernible effects on academic achievement, social interactions, observed individual behavior, or emotional status for elementary students. The null findings across all four outcome domains are notable given the program's widespread adoption in U.S. schools. |
| 606 | [Xtreme Reading](https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/713) | report | Xtreme Reading is a supplemental literacy curriculum for struggling readers in grades 6–12 designed to improve vocabulary, decoding, fluency, and reading comprehension through teacher-led whole-group instruction, cooperative group work, paired practice, and independent practice along with social skills training and motivational components. The WWC reviewed 3 eligible studies, with 2 meeting standards, and found no discernible effects on comprehension and general literacy achievement for struggling readers in grades 6–12. The consistent null findings across both outcome domains examined suggest limited evidence of the program's effectiveness for this population. |
| 607 | [Math Expressions](https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/715) | report | Math Expressions is a mathematics curriculum for pre-K through grade 6 that builds students' conceptual understanding through real-world situations, visual supports including drawings and manipulatives, multiple problem-solving approaches, and opportunities for students to explain their mathematical thinking. The WWC reviewed 3 eligible studies, with 1 meeting standards, and found no discernible effects on general mathematics achievement for elementary students compared with other mathematics curricula used in the comparison schools. The single qualifying study limits the strength of conclusions that can be drawn about the program's effectiveness. |
| 608 | [University of Chicago School Mathematics Project (UCSMP) Transitions Math](https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/717) | report | University of Chicago School Mathematics Project (UCSMP) Transitions/Pre-Transition Math is a core mathematics curriculum for grades 6–9 featuring an inquiry-based approach with active learning, hands-on and small-group activities, covering arithmetic, algebra, geometry, probability, and statistics at progressively advanced levels across the two course variants. The WWC reviewed 4 eligible studies, with 3 meeting standards, and found no discernible effects on general mathematics achievement or algebra outcomes for students in grades 6–9 compared with other curricula used in study schools. The relatively strong evidence base (3 qualifying studies) with null findings provides a fairly confident negative conclusion about this curriculum's comparative effectiveness. |
| 610 | [LASER — Science Education Reform (Grades 3–8)](https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/721) | report | Leadership and Assistance for Science Education Reform (LASER) builds capacity for implementing inquiry-based science curricula through leadership development institutes, professional development for teachers, instructional materials access, assessment support, and partnerships with scientists and community leaders, targeting grades 3–8. The WWC reviewed 2 eligible studies, with 1 meeting standards, and found no discernible effects on general science achievement compared with standard instruction. The no-discernible-effects finding for this systemic capacity-building approach suggests that regional infrastructure development alone may not translate to measurable student achievement gains. |
| 613 | [System of Least Prompts](https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/685) | report | System of Least Prompts (SLP), also known as least-to-most prompting, is an instructional practice for students with intellectual disabilities in which teachers establish a structured hierarchy of prompts starting with the least assistive and increasing support until the student performs the skill correctly. The WWC found no qualifying group design studies, and single-case design studies did not reach the threshold required for an evidence rating in any outcome domain. Despite the absence of group-design evidence, SLP is widely used in special education for skill acquisition across academic and functional tasks. |
| 614 | [Harlem Children's Zone Promise Academy Charter Schools](https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/687) | report | Harlem Children's Zone (HCZ) Promise Academy Charter Schools is a non-profit initiative providing community services and operating two public K–12 charter schools featuring extended school days and years, an academic and arts focus, student progress monitoring, teacher quality initiatives, and community support services including counseling and medical care. As of January 2018, the WWC found no studies meeting their design standards and therefore cannot draw conclusions about the effectiveness or ineffectiveness of this intervention. The absence of qualifying evidence reflects the challenges of applying group design standards to unique charter school models with small catchment populations. |
| 615 | [ACT Aspire — Transition to College](https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/674) | report | ACT Aspire is a longitudinal, systematic assessment system for grades 3 through early high school that monitors students' preparation for high school studies and readiness for college and career across five subject areas, designed to support ongoing instructional adjustment toward college and career readiness goals. As of May 2017, the WWC found no studies meeting their design standards within the Transition to College review protocol and therefore cannot draw research-based conclusions about ACT Aspire's effectiveness in improving college transition outcomes. The program's assessment-based design distinguishes it from instructional interventions, reflecting the WWC's broader interest in evaluating tools used to support educational decision-making. |
| 616 | [Prentice Hall Literature (1989–2005)](https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/681) | report | Prentice Hall Literature (1989–2005) is an English language arts curriculum for grades 6–12 emphasizing reading, writing, listening, viewing, speaking, and language skills through thematic organization, genre-focused units, and supplementary materials for differentiated instruction. As of the WWC review, no studies were found meeting design standards within the Adolescent Literacy review protocol, preventing the WWC from drawing research-based conclusions about the program's effectiveness. The curriculum's long publication history and widespread adoption contrast with the complete absence of qualifying rigorous evaluations. |
| 617 | [Reciprocal Teaching — Students with Learning Disabilities](https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/626) | report | Reciprocal Teaching is an interactive instructional method for improving reading comprehension in which the teacher and students take turns leading a dialogue regarding segments of the text, teaching four core strategies: generating questions, summarizing, clarifying, and predicting, reviewed here for students with specific learning disabilities. The WWC found no studies meeting their evidence standards for this population within the relevant review protocol and therefore cannot draw conclusions about the effectiveness or ineffectiveness of Reciprocal Teaching for students with learning disabilities. The lack of qualifying evidence is notable given the intervention's prominent theoretical basis and widespread discussion in the reading research literature. |
| 618 | [UCSMP Advanced Algebra](https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/644) | report | University of Chicago School Mathematics Project (UCSMP) Advanced Algebra is a core secondary mathematics curriculum emphasizing problem solving, real-world applications, and the use of technology, featuring a student-centered approach with active learning that incorporates reading and flexible lesson structures. As of May 2016, the WWC found no studies meeting their design standards within the Secondary Mathematics review protocol, and therefore cannot draw research-based conclusions about the program's effectiveness or ineffectiveness. The UCSMP curriculum family includes multiple courses, each reviewed separately, with none of the individual courses having qualifying evaluative evidence in the secondary mathematics protocol. |
| 620 | [Lexia Core5 Reading](https://evidenceforessa.org/program/lexia-core5-reading/) | report | Lexia Core5 Reading is a blended learning program for PreK–5 that provides explicit, systematic reading instruction through personalized learning paths adapted to individual student skill gaps, combining online instruction with embedded assessments to help educators customize and track student progress. Across four studies involving over 17,000 students, Core5 students showed an average reading achievement effect size of +0.16 compared to matched comparison groups. Rated Moderate by Evidence for ESSA. |
| 621 | [SIPPS (Systematic Instruction in Phonological Awareness, Phonics, and Sight Words)](https://evidenceforessa.org/program/sipps-systematic-instruction-in-phonological-awareness-phonics-and-sight-words-2/) | report | SIPPS is a structured-literacy reading curriculum using explicit instruction in phonological awareness, phonics, and sight words to support both new and struggling readers across three developmental levels, with flexible grouping based on individual student needs. Rated Moderate by Evidence for ESSA. |
| 622 | [Expository Reading and Writing Course (ERWC)](https://evidenceforessa.org/program/expository-reading-and-writing-course-erwc/) | report | The Expository Reading and Writing Course (ERWC) is a 12th-grade college-readiness program designed to prepare high school seniors to enter California State University and community colleges without needing remediation in English, providing curriculum materials and several days of professional development and coaching. Teachers focus instruction on text analysis, critical thinking, discussions, oral language development, and writing across genres. | 623 | [The Superkids Reading Program](https://evidenceforessa.org/program/the-superkids-reading-program/) | report | The Superkids Reading Program is a phonics-based beginning reading curriculum for grades K–2 that emphasizes phonemic awareness, phonics, vocabulary, comprehension, writing, and spelling. | 624 | [Amira](https://evidenceforessa.org/program/amira/) | report | Amira is an AI-powered reading tutor for grades K–4 that provides personalized instruction, assesses oral reading fluency, and generates diagnostic reports for teachers and parents. | 625 | [Imagine Español](https://evidenceforessa.org/program/imagine-learning-imagine-espanol/) | report | Imagine Español is a personalized learning program for Pre-K through grade 6 that accelerates Spanish language and literacy development through engaging, culturally diverse content, with demonstrated gains in both Spanish and English reading proficiency. | 653 | [PAX Good Behavior Game — Math](https://evidenceforessa.org/program/pax-good-behavior-game-math/) | report | PAX Good Behavior Game – Math is a classroom behavior management system for grades 1–2 that divides students into teams and uses group contingencies—awarding check marks for rule violations—to promote on-task behavior during math instruction. Key findings indicate that inclusion neither increases nor decreases learning and psychosocial adjustment on average, with effect sizes varying considerably across studies. The authors conclude that placement decisions should be individualized rather than following a one-size-fits-all approach. |

Average student achievement was higher in both reading and math at year-round schools, with gains roughly equivalent to one month of learning, similar to documented summer learning loss. | 944 | [Relative Effectiveness of Conditional and Unconditional Cash Transfers for Schooling Outcomes in Developing Countries](https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/effectiveness-of-cash-transfers-for-schooling-outcomes) | review | This Campbell systematic review evaluated 35 studies examining conditional and unconditional cash transfer programmes' effects on education outcomes in low- and middle-income countries. Both program types increase school enrollment compared to no intervention, though effects on learning outcomes remain limited. The analysis reveals that conditions that are strictly monitored and enforced produce substantially larger enrollment gains, increasing odds by 60% versus under 20% for programmes without conditions. |

| 947 | [Interventions in Developing Nations for Improving Primary and Secondary School Enrollments](https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/improving-school-enrolment-developing-nations) | review | This systematic review examined 73 randomized controlled trials and quasi-experiments published through December 2009 to assess interventions in low- and middle-income countries on student enrollment, attendance, graduation, and progression. Results showed positive effects across all outcomes, with enrollment showing the largest average effect size (d=.18) and infrastructure interventions for new schools demonstrating the strongest results (d=.44). | 948 | [Social Skills Groups for People Aged 6 to 21 with Autism Spectrum Disorders](https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/social-skills-groups-people-aged-6-to-21-autism-spectrum-disorders) | review | This systematic review examined five randomized controlled trials involving 196 participants to evaluate whether social skills groups help individuals aged 6-21 with autism spectrum disorder. Findings indicate some evidence that social skills groups improve overall social competence and friendship quality, though no significant improvements were found in emotion recognition, understanding of idioms, or most quality-of-life outcomes. The authors conclude that while social skills groups show promise for enhancing social competence, additional rigorous research is needed to establish more definitive conclusions. |
| 949 | [School Feeding for Improving the Physical and Psychosocial Health of Disadvantaged Students](https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/school-feeding-disadvantaged-students-improving-health) | review | This systematic review evaluated whether school feeding programs enhance health outcomes for economically disadvantaged pupils, analyzing 18 studies examining weight gain, height, school attendance, and academic achievement. Results indicated modest positive effects, particularly in lower-income countries where children gained approximately 0.39-0.71 kg over study periods and showed improved attendance and math performance. | 950 | [The Effects of School-Based Social Information Processing Interventions on Aggressive Behavior, Part I: Universal Programs](https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/school-based-interventions-aggressive-behaviour-part1) | review | This systematic review analyzed 73 studies of universal classroom programs aimed at improving children's ability to interpret social situations to reduce aggressive and disruptive behaviour. Findings indicate that brief, intensive interventions of 8-16 weeks prove more effective than extended year-long programs, with social information processing interventions training children through six cognitive stages from encoding cues to behavioral enactment. The research demonstrates that emphasizing thought patterns rather than direct behavior modification strengthens children's general social competencies and reduces aggression across diverse populations. |
| 951 | [The Effects of School-Based Social Information Processing Interventions on Aggressive Behavior, Part II: Selected/Indicated Pull-Out Programs](https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/school-based-interventions-aggressive-behaviour-part2) | review | This Campbell systematic review examined school-based education programmes targeting children's ability to interpret social situations to reduce aggressive behaviour, covering 47 studies of interventions delivered to selected children with behavioural problems or at-risk populations. Students who participated exhibited notably reduced aggressive and disruptive conduct compared to non-participants, with particularly strong effects for pull-out programmes serving at-risk groups outside regular classrooms. This companion review to Part I focuses specifically on targeted interventions rather than universal programs and demonstrates stronger effects for higher-risk populations. |
